House File 317 - Introduced


                                 HOUSE FILE 

                                 HOUSE FILE 
                                 HOUSE FILE                                  HOUSE FILE                                  BY  DAWSON, HEDDENS, and
                                     WESSEL=KROESCHELL

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act relating to the provision of telehealth services by
  2    mental health professionals relative to insurance coverage
  3    and reimbursement under the medical assistance program.
  4 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 1131YH (10) 86
    pf/nh

PAG LIN

  1  1    Section 1.    4 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:

  1  1    Section 1.      TLSB 1131YH (10) 86
    pf/nh

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.      pf/nh

PAG LIN



  1  1    Section 1.  

  1  1    Section 1.  
  1  1    Section 1.    1  1    Section 1.    1  2 provided by mental health professionals.
  1  3    1.  Notwithstanding the uniformity of treatment requirements
  1  4 of section 514C.6, a contract, policy, or plan providing for
  1  5 third=party payment or prepayment for health, medical, or
  1  6 surgical coverage benefits shall not require face=to=face
  1  7 contact between a mental health professional and a patient as a
  1  8 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  1  9 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  1 10 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  1 11 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  1 12 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  1 13 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  1 14 for the purposes of coverage.
  1 15    2.  This section shall not be interpreted as preventing
  1 16 a third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  1 17 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  1 18 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  1 19 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  1 20 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  1 21 same health care service.
  1 22    3.  The provisions of this section shall apply to all of the
  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh

  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic

  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.

  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1  6 surgical coverage benefits shall not require face=to=face
  1  7 contact between a mental health professional and a patient as a
  1  8 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  1  9 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  1 10 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  1 11 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  1 12 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  1 13 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  1 14 for the purposes of coverage.
  1 15    2.  This section shall not be interpreted as preventing
  1 16 a third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  1 17 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  1 18 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  1 19 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  1 20 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  1 21 same health care service.
  1 22    3.  The provisions of this section shall apply to all of the
  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.

  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.

  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1 10 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  1 11 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  1 12 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  1 13 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  1 14 for the purposes of coverage.
  1 15    2.  This section shall not be interpreted as preventing
  1 16 a third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  1 17 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  1 18 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  1 19 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  1 20 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  1 21 same health care service.
  1 22    3.  The provisions of this section shall apply to all of the
  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.

  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1 14 for the purposes of coverage.
  1 15    2.  This section shall not be interpreted as preventing
  1 16 a third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  1 17 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  1 18 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  1 19 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  1 20 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  1 21 same health care service.
  1 22    3.  The provisions of this section shall apply to all of the
  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules

  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.

  1 19 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  1 20 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  1 21 same health care service.

  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.

  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,

  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined

  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1 23 following classes of third=party payment provider contracts,
  1 24 policies, or plans delivered, issued for delivery, continued,
  1 25 or renewed in this state on or after January 1, 2016:
  1 26    a.  Individual or group accident and sickness insurance
  1 27 providing coverage on an expense=incurred basis.
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.

  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1 28    b.  An individual or group hospital or medical service
  1 29 contract issued pursuant to chapter 509, 514, or 514A.
  1 30    c.  An individual or group health maintenance organization
  1 31 contract regulated under chapter 514B.
  1 32    d.  An individual or group Medicare supplemental policy,
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a

  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.

  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  1 33 unless coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal
  1 34 law.
  1 35    e.  A plan established pursuant to chapter 509A for public
  2  1 employees.
  2  2    4.  This section shall not apply to accident=only, specified
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.

  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  2  3 disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital confinement
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.
  2 26    Sec. 2.  MEDICAID PROGRAM ==== REIMBURSEMENT FOR
  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  2 30 The rules shall provide that face=to=face contact between a
  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
  3  7                           EXPLANATION
  3  8 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  3  9 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  3 10    This bill relates to telehealth services provided by a
  3 11 mental health professional.
  3 12    The bill provides that beginning January 1, 2016, a
  3 13 contract, policy, or plan providing for third=party payment or
  3 14 prepayment for health, medical, or surgical coverage benefits
  3 15 shall not require face=to=face contact between a mental health
  3 16 professional and a patient as a prerequisite for payment
  3 17 for services appropriately provided through telehealth in
  3 18 accordance with generally accepted health care practices and
  3 19 standards prevailing in the applicable professional community
  3 20 at the time the services are provided.  Health care services
  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  2  4 indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term care, basic
  2  5 hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage as defined
  2  6 by the commissioner, disability income insurance coverage,
  2  7 coverage issued as a supplement to liability insurance,
  2  8 workers' compensation or similar insurance, or automobile
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined

  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains

  3 21 provided through in=person consultations or through telehealth
  3 22 shall be treated as equivalent services for the purposes of
  3 23 coverage.
  3 24    The provision is not to be interpreted as preventing a
  3 25 third=party payment provider from imposing deductibles or
  3 26 copayment or coinsurance requirements for a health care service
  3 27 provided through telehealth if the deductible, copayment, or
  3 28 coinsurance does not exceed the deductible, copayment, or
  3 29 coinsurance applicable to an in=person consultation for the
  3 30 same health care service. The section applies to individual
  3 31 or group accident and sickness insurance providing coverage
  3 32 on an expense=incurred basis; an individual or group hospital
  3 33 or medical service contract issued pursuant to Code chapter
  3 34 509, 514, or 514A; an individual or group health maintenance
  3 35 organization contract regulated under Code chapter 514B; an
  4  1 individual or group Medicare supplemental policy, unless
  4  2 coverage pursuant to such policy is preempted by federal law;
  4  3 and a plan established pursuant to Code chapter 509A for public
  4  4 employees. The provision does not apply to accident=only,
  4  5 specified disease, short=term hospital or medical, hospital
  4  6 confinement indemnity, credit, dental, vision, long=term
  4  7 care, basic hospital, and medical=surgical expense coverage
  4  8 as defined by the commissioner, disability income insurance
  4  9 coverage, coverage issued as a supplement to liability
  4 10 insurance, workers' compensation or similar insurance, or
  4 11 automobile medical payment insurance.
  4 12    The commissioner of insurance is directed to adopt rules
  4 13 pursuant to Code chapter 17A as necessary to administer the
  4 14 provision.  The bill defines "mental health professional" and
  4 15 "telehealth" or "telehealth services".
  4 16    The bill directs the department of human services to adopt
  4 17 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  4 18 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.
  4 19 The rules are to provide that face=to=face contact between a
  4 20 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  4 21 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  4 22 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  4 23 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  4 24 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  4 25 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  4 26 or through telehealth are to be treated as equivalent services
  4 27 for the purposes of reimbursement.
       LSB 1131YH (10) 86
       pf/nh
  2  9 medical payment insurance.
  2 10    5.  As used in this section:
  2 11    a.  "Mental health professional" means the same as defined
  2 12 in section 228.1.
  2 13    b.  "Telehealth" or "telehealth services", as it pertains
  2 14 to the delivery of health care services, means synchronous
  2 15 video conferencing, remote patient monitoring, transmission
  2 16 of asynchronous health images, or other health transmissions
  2 17 supported by mobile devices, or other telecommunications
  2 18 technology used for the purpose of diagnosis, consultation,
  2 19 treatment, transfer of medical data, or exchange of medical
  2 20 education information by means of audio, video, or data
  2 21 communications. "Telehealth" or "telehealth services" does not
  2 22 include an audio=only telephone call, electronic mail message,
  2 23 or facsimile transmission.
  2 24    6.  The commissioner of insurance shall adopt rules pursuant
  2 25 to chapter 17A as necessary to administer this section.

  2 27 TELEHEALTH.  The department of human services shall adopt
  2 28 rules to provide for coverage of telehealth services provided
  2 29 by a mental health professional under the Medicaid program.

  2 31 mental health professional and a patient is not required as a
  2 32 prerequisite for payment for services appropriately provided
  2 33 through telehealth in accordance with generally accepted health
  2 34 care practices and standards prevailing in the applicable
  2 35 professional community at the time the services are provided.
  3  1 Health care services provided through in=person consultations
  3  2 or through telehealth shall be treated as equivalent services
  3  3 for the purposes of reimbursement.  For the purposes of this
  3  4 section, "mental health professional" and "telehealth" or
  3  5 "telehealth services" means the same as defined in section
  3  6 514C.30, as enacted in this Act.
